					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Ancient Syrian city</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the star also named Ebla, see <a href="/wiki/HD_218566" title="HD 218566">HD 218566</a>. For eBLA, see <a href="/wiki/Biologics_license_application" title="Biologics license application">Biologics license application</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electronic_common_technical_document" title="Electronic common technical document">Electronic common technical document</a>.</div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Elbe" title="Elbe">Elbe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elba" title="Elba">Elba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ebola" title="Ebola">Ebola</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Ablah" title="Ablah">Ablah</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

<p><b>Ebla</b> (<a href="/wiki/Sumerian_language" title="Sumerian language">Sumerian</a>: <span style="font-size:125%;font-family:&#39;Segoe UI Historic&#39;,&#39;Akkadian&#39;,&#39;Noto Sans Cuneiform&#39;,&#39;Noto Sans Sumero-Akkadian Cuneiform&#39;;" title="cuneiform text" lang="und-Xsux">𒌈𒆷</span> <i>eb₂-la</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">إبلا</span>, modern: <span title="Arabic-language text"><span lang="ar" dir="rtl">تل مرديخ</span></span>, <b>Tell Mardikh</b>) was one of the earliest kingdoms in <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>. Its remains constitute a <a href="/wiki/Tell_(archaeology)" title="Tell (archaeology)">tell</a> located about 55&#160;km (34&#160;mi) southwest of <a href="/wiki/Aleppo" title="Aleppo">Aleppo</a> near the village of <a href="/wiki/Mardikh" title="Mardikh">Mardikh</a>. Ebla was an important center throughout the <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/3rd_millennium_BC" title="3rd millennium BC">3rd millennium <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span></a></span> and in the first half of the <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/2nd_millennium_BC" title="2nd millennium BC">2nd millennium <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span></a>.</span> Its discovery proved the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a> was a center of ancient, centralized civilization equal to <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Egypt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> and ruled out the view that the latter two were the only important centers in the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Near_East" title="Ancient Near East">Near East</a> during the Early <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>. The first Eblaite kingdom has been described as the first recorded world power.
</p><p>Starting as a small settlement in the Early Bronze Age (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;3500</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>), Ebla developed into a trading empire and later into an expansionist power that imposed its hegemony over much of northern and eastern Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ebla was destroyed during the <span class="nowrap">23rd century <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>.</span> It was then rebuilt and was mentioned in the records of the <a href="/wiki/Third_Dynasty_of_Ur" title="Third Dynasty of Ur">Third Dynasty of Ur</a>. The second Ebla was a continuation of the first, ruled by a new royal dynasty. It was destroyed at the end of the <span class="nowrap">3rd millennium <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>,</span> which paved the way for the <a href="/wiki/Amorite" class="mw-redirect" title="Amorite">Amorite</a> tribes to settle in the city, forming the third Ebla. The third kingdom also flourished as a trade center; it became a subject and an ally of <a href="/wiki/Yamhad" title="Yamhad">Yamhad</a> (modern-day Aleppo) until its final destruction by the <a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites">Hittite</a> king <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Mursili_I" title="Mursili I">Mursili I</a></span> in <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1600</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>.
</p><p>Ebla maintained its prosperity through a vast trading network. Artifacts from <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">Sumer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> and as far as <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> were recovered from the city's palaces. The kingdom had its own language, <a href="/wiki/Eblaite_language" title="Eblaite language">Eblaite</a>, and the political organization of Ebla had features different from the Sumerian model. Women enjoyed a special status, and the queen had major influence in the state and religious affairs. The pantheon of gods was mainly north Semitic and included deities exclusive to Ebla. The city was excavated from 1964 and became famous for the <a href="/wiki/Ebla_tablets" title="Ebla tablets">Ebla tablets</a>, an archive of about 20,000&#160;<a href="/wiki/Cuneiform" title="Cuneiform">cuneiform</a> tablets found there, dated to 2500&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>–2350&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Written in both <a href="/wiki/Sumerian_language" title="Sumerian language">Sumerian</a> and Eblaite and using the <a href="/wiki/Cuneiform" title="Cuneiform">cuneiform</a>, the archive has allowed a better understanding of the Sumerian language and provided important information over the political organization and social customs of the mid-3rd millennium&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>'s Levant.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Etymology">Etymology</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ebla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The word "Ebla" means "white rock" and may refer to the limestone outcrop on which the city was built.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDolce2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA248_248&#93;_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDolce2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA248_248]-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMantelliniMicalePeyronel2013&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA182_182&#93;_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMantelliniMicalePeyronel2013[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA182_182]-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ebla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Chalcolithic">Chalcolithic</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ebla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Chalcolithic"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In the central mound, finds from the Late Ubaid and Late Chalcolithic has been found.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Early_Bronze">Early Bronze</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ebla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early Bronze"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Ebla was first settled around 3500&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamblin2006&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbiyDDd0uKGMCpgPT239_241&#93;_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamblin2006[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbiyDDd0uKGMCpgPT239_241]-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShaw1999&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid8HKDtlPuM2oCpgPA211_211&#93;_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShaw1999[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid8HKDtlPuM2oCpgPA211_211]-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> its growth was supported by many satellite agricultural settlements.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamblin2006&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbiyDDd0uKGMCpgPT239_241&#93;_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamblin2006[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbiyDDd0uKGMCpgPT239_241]-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The city benefited from its role as an <a href="/wiki/Entrep%C3%B4t" title="Entrepôt">entrepôt</a> of growing international trade, which probably began with an increased demand for wool in <a href="/wiki/Sumer" title="Sumer">Sumer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamblin2006&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbiyDDd0uKGMCpgPT239_241&#93;_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamblin2006[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbiyDDd0uKGMCpgPT239_241]-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Archaeologists designate this early habitation period "Mardikh&#160;I"; it ended around 3000&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeick2009&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidjhbSbuplQ28CpgPA54_54&#93;_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeick2009[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidjhbSbuplQ28CpgPA54_54]-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Mardikh I is followed by the first and second kingdoms era between about 3000 and 2000&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>, designated "Mardikh II".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatthiae2013a&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA37_37&#93;_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatthiae2013a[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA37_37]-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/I._J._Gelb" class="mw-redirect" title="I. J. Gelb">I. J. Gelb</a> considered Ebla as part of the <a href="/wiki/Kish_civilization" title="Kish civilization">Kish civilization</a>, which was a cultural entity of <a href="/wiki/East_Semitic_languages" title="East Semitic languages">East Semitic</a>-speaking populations that stretched from the center of Mesopotamia to the western Levant.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_De_Mieroop2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid6lDgYxV0DN8CpgPA133_133&#93;_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_De_Mieroop2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid6lDgYxV0DN8CpgPA133_133]-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="First_kingdom">First kingdom</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ebla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: First kingdom"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

<td style="border:0; padding:0; vertical-align:middle; text-align:right;"><a href="/wiki/The_second_kingdom_of_Mari" class="mw-redirect" title="The second kingdom of Mari">The second kingdom of Mari</a>
</td>
<td style="border:0; padding:0; vertical-align:middle;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/Mari,_Syria#The_second_kingdom" title="Mari, Syria"><img alt="Second Mariote kingdom" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Second_Mariote_kingdom.png/50px-Second_Mariote_kingdom.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="32" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Second_Mariote_kingdom.png/75px-Second_Mariote_kingdom.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Second_Mariote_kingdom.png/100px-Second_Mariote_kingdom.png 2x" data-file-width="1326" data-file-height="842" /></a></span>
</td></tr>









































</tbody></table>
</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Today part of</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>During the first kingdom period between about 3000 and 2300&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>, Ebla was the most prominent kingdom among the Syrian states, especially during the second half of the 3rd millennium&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>, which is known as "the age of the archives" after the Ebla tablets.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatthiae2013a&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA37_37&#93;_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatthiae2013a[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA37_37]-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p><b>Mardiikh IIA</b>: The early period between 3000 and 2400&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span> is designated "Mardikh IIA".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatthiae2013a&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA37_37&#93;_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatthiae2013a[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA37_37]-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEÖkse2011&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidTY3t4y_L5SQCpgPA268_268&#93;_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEÖkse2011[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidTY3t4y_L5SQCpgPA268_268]-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> General knowledge about the city's history prior to the written archives is obtained through excavations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDolce2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA250_250&#93;_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDolce2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA250_250]-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The first stages of Mardikh&#160;IIA is identified with building&#160;"CC",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDolce2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA247_247&#93;_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDolce2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA247_247]-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and structures that form a part of building "G2",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDolce2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA246_246&#93;_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDolce2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA246_246]-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which was apparently a royal palace built <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2700</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamblin2006&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbiyDDd0uKGMCpgPT239_241&#93;_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamblin2006[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbiyDDd0uKGMCpgPT239_241]-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDolce2008&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidJ9eZToFfVJ0CpgPA66_66&#93;_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDolce2008[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidJ9eZToFfVJ0CpgPA66_66]-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Toward the end of this period, a <a href="/wiki/Mari,_Syria#Mari–Ebla_war" title="Mari, Syria">hundred years' war</a> with <a href="/wiki/Mari,_Syria" title="Mari, Syria">Mari</a> started.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENadali2007&#91;httpswwwacademiaedu619545Davide_Nadali_2007_Monuments_of_war_war_of_monuments_Some_considerations_on_commemorating_war_in_the_Third_Millennium_BC_349&#93;_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENadali2007[httpswwwacademiaedu619545Davide_Nadali_2007_Monuments_of_war_war_of_monuments_Some_considerations_on_commemorating_war_in_the_Third_Millennium_BC_349]-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA79_79&#93;_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA79_79]-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Mari gained the upper hand through the actions of its king <a href="/wiki/Sa%CA%BFumu" title="Saʿumu">Saʿumu</a>, who conquered many of Ebla's cities.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELiverani2013&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0d1JAgAAQBAJpgPA119_119&#93;_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELiverani2013[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0d1JAgAAQBAJpgPA119_119]-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the mid-25th century&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>, king <a href="/wiki/Kun-Damu" title="Kun-Damu">Kun-Damu</a> defeated Mari, but the state's power declined following his reign.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDolce2008&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidJ9eZToFfVJ0CpgPA68_68&#93;_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDolce2008[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidJ9eZToFfVJ0CpgPA68_68]-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ebla_-_DecArch_-_2-126.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Ebla_-_DecArch_-_2-126.jpg/220px-Ebla_-_DecArch_-_2-126.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Ebla_-_DecArch_-_2-126.jpg/330px-Ebla_-_DecArch_-_2-126.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Ebla_-_DecArch_-_2-126.jpg/440px-Ebla_-_DecArch_-_2-126.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4416" data-file-height="2944" /></a><figcaption>Royal palace "G"</figcaption></figure>
<p><b>Mardikh IIB1</b>: The archive period, which is designated "Mardikh IIB1", lasted from <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2400</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span> until <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2300</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatthiae2013a&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA37_37&#93;_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatthiae2013a[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA37_37]-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The end of the period is known as the "first destruction",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatthiae2013a&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA38_38&#93;_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatthiae2013a[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA38_38]-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> mainly referring to the destruction of the royal palace (called palace&#160;"G" and built over the earlier "G2"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour1992&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidrXcvrnUF36EC_19&#93;_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour1992[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidrXcvrnUF36EC_19]-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and much of the acropolis.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA74_74&#93;_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA74_74]-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the archive period, Ebla had political and military dominance over the other Syrian city-states of northern and eastern Syria, which are mentioned in the archives.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPettinato1981&#91;httpsarchiveorgdetailsarchivesofeblaan00pett_105&#93;_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPettinato1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsarchivesofeblaan00pett_105]-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Most of the tablets, which date from that period, are about economic matters but also include royal letters and diplomatic documents.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBryce2014&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidq8Z7AgAAQBAJpgPA15_15&#93;_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBryce2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidq8Z7AgAAQBAJpgPA15_15]-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The written archives do not date from before <a href="/wiki/Igrish-Halam" title="Igrish-Halam">Igrish-Halam</a>'s reign,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETonietti2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid-H3iYPUc97YCpgPA69_69&#93;_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETonietti2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid-H3iYPUc97YCpgPA69_69]-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which saw Ebla paying tribute to Mari,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENadali2007&#91;httpswwwacademiaedu619545Davide_Nadali_2007_Monuments_of_war_war_of_monuments_Some_considerations_on_commemorating_war_in_the_Third_Millennium_BC_350&#93;_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENadali2007[httpswwwacademiaedu619545Davide_Nadali_2007_Monuments_of_war_war_of_monuments_Some_considerations_on_commemorating_war_in_the_Third_Millennium_BC_350]-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and an extensive invasion of Eblaite cities in the middle Euphrates region led by the Mariote king <a href="/wiki/Iblul-Il" title="Iblul-Il">Iblul-Il</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoux1992&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidklZX8B_RzzYCpgPT200_200&#93;_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoux1992[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidklZX8B_RzzYCpgPT200_200]-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeliu2003&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidIN9_IRYKKUMCpgPA40_40&#93;_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeliu2003[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidIN9_IRYKKUMCpgPA40_40]-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ebla recovered under King <a href="/wiki/Irkab-Damu" title="Irkab-Damu">Irkab-Damu</a> in about 2340&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>; becoming prosperous and launching a successful counter-offensive against Mari.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPodany2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid_ez3ih5JgzUCpgPA24_24&#93;_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPodany2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid_ez3ih5JgzUCpgPA24_24]-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECooper2006&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidySjxzVWf120CpgPA64_64&#93;_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECooper2006[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidySjxzVWf120CpgPA64_64]-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Irkab-Damu concluded a peace and trading treaty with <a href="/wiki/Abarsal" title="Abarsal">Abarsal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArchi2011&#91;httpswwwjstororgdiscover105615jcunestud630005_5&#93;_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArchi2011[httpswwwjstororgdiscover105615jcunestud630005_5]-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This <a href="/wiki/Treaty_between_Ebla_and_Abarsal" title="Treaty between Ebla and Abarsal">Treaty between Ebla and Abarsal</a> is one of the earliest-recorded treaties in history.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeff2014&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidu5DzAgAAQBAJpgPA14_14&#93;_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeff2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidu5DzAgAAQBAJpgPA14_14]-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading5"><h5 id="Geography">Geography</h5><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ebla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>At its greatest extent, Ebla controlled an area roughly half the size of modern Syria,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamblin2006&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbiyDDd0uKGMCpgPT240_242&#93;_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamblin2006[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbiyDDd0uKGMCpgPT240_242]-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> from <a href="/wiki/Urshu" title="Urshu">Ursa'um</a> in the north,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA101_101&#93;_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA101_101]-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> to the area around <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a> in the south,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETubb1998&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidGH-n4ctvlDYCpgPA39_39&#93;_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETubb1998[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidGH-n4ctvlDYCpgPA39_39]-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and from <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia#Origins" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Coastal_Mountain_Range" title="Syrian Coastal Mountain Range">coastal mountains</a> in the west,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAubet2001&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidB7SLWT2vpNcCpgPA18_18&#93;_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAubet2001[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidB7SLWT2vpNcCpgPA18_18]-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour1981&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid1A0OgvXfHlQCpgPA4_4&#93;_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour1981[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid1A0OgvXfHlQCpgPA4_4]-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> to <a href="/wiki/Haddu" title="Haddu">Haddu</a> in the east.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArchi2011&#91;httpswwwjstororgdiscover105615jcunestud630005_5&#93;_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArchi2011[httpswwwjstororgdiscover105615jcunestud630005_5]-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECooper2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid46SmAwAAQBAJpgPT133_89&#93;_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECooper2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid46SmAwAAQBAJpgPT133_89]-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Large parts of the kingdom were under the direct control of the king and were administered by governors; the rest consisted of vassal kingdoms.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamblin2006&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbiyDDd0uKGMCpgPT240_242&#93;_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamblin2006[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbiyDDd0uKGMCpgPT240_242]-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> One of the most important of these vassals was <a href="/wiki/Armi_(Syria)" title="Armi (Syria)">Armi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPettinato1991&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidK4JtAAAAMAAJ_135&#93;_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPettinato1991[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidK4JtAAAAMAAJ_135]-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which is the city most often mentioned in the Ebla tablets.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOttoBiga2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA486_486&#93;_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOttoBiga2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA486_486]-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ebla had more than sixty vassal kingdoms and city-states,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA66_66&#93;_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA66_66]-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Khashshum" class="mw-redirect" title="Khashshum">Hazuwan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweyhat" title="Sweyhat">Burman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emar" title="Emar">Emar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halabiye" title="Halabiye">Halabitu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zalabiye" title="Zalabiye">Salbatu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECooper2006&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidySjxzVWf120CpgPA64_64&#93;_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECooper2006[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidySjxzVWf120CpgPA64_64]-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECooper2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid46SmAwAAQBAJpgPT133_89&#93;_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECooper2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid46SmAwAAQBAJpgPT133_89]-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA83_83&#93;_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA83_83]-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>According to Archi, these are "the twelve Syrian cities long allied with Ebla that (presumably) assisted in some way during the expedition against Mari: NIrar, Ra’ak, Burman, Dub, Emar, Garmu, Lumnan, Ibubu, <a href="/wiki/Urshu" title="Urshu">Ursaum</a>, Utik, Kakmium, and Iritum (<a href="/wiki/Irridu" title="Irridu">Irridu</a>)." Furthermore, the following cities were under Ebla’s hegemony at that time, and annually delivered tribute: Dub, Dulu, <a href="/wiki/Harran" title="Harran">Harran</a>, Ibubu, Iritum, Kablul, Sanapzugum, Ursaum, and Utik.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArchi201117_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArchi201117-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The vizier was the king's chief official.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA59_59&#93;_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA59_59]-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The holder of the office possessed great authority; the most powerful vizier was <a href="/wiki/Ibrium" title="Ibrium">Ibrium</a>, who campaigned against Abarsal during the term of his predecessor Arrukum.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELiverani2013&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0d1JAgAAQBAJpgPA123_123&#93;_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELiverani2013[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0d1JAgAAQBAJpgPA123_123]-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ibrium held office for 18 years with warfare occurring in all but one year.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the reign of <a href="/wiki/Isar-Damu" title="Isar-Damu">Isar-Damu</a>, Ebla continued the war against Mari, which defeated Ebla's ally <a href="/wiki/Tell_Brak#Kingdom_of_Nagar" title="Tell Brak">Nagar</a>, blocking trade routes between Ebla and southern Mesopotamia via upper Mesopotamia.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENadali2007&#91;httpswwwacademiaedu619545Davide_Nadali_2007_Monuments_of_war_war_of_monuments_Some_considerations_on_commemorating_war_in_the_Third_Millennium_BC_350&#93;_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENadali2007[httpswwwacademiaedu619545Davide_Nadali_2007_Monuments_of_war_war_of_monuments_Some_considerations_on_commemorating_war_in_the_Third_Millennium_BC_350]-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ebla conducted regular military campaigns against rebellious vassals,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELiverani2013&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0d1JAgAAQBAJpgPA123_123&#93;_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELiverani2013[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0d1JAgAAQBAJpgPA123_123]-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> including several attacks on Armi,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOttoBiga2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA484_484&#93;_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOttoBiga2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA484_484]-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOttoBiga2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA485_485&#93;_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOttoBiga2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA485_485]-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOttoBiga2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA486_486&#93;_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOttoBiga2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA486_486]-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and a campaign against the southern region of <a href="/wiki/Ib%27al" title="Ib&#39;al">Ib'al</a> – close to <a href="/wiki/Qatna" title="Qatna">Qatna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELiverani2013&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0d1JAgAAQBAJpgPA123_123&#93;_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELiverani2013[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0d1JAgAAQBAJpgPA123_123]-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELiverani2013&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0d1JAgAAQBAJpgPA121_121&#93;_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELiverani2013[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0d1JAgAAQBAJpgPA121_121]-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In order to settle the war with Mari, Isar-Damu allied with Nagar and <a href="/wiki/Kish_(Sumer)" title="Kish (Sumer)">Kish</a>. Some scholars have suggested that the Kish in question was not the Mesopotamian city but rather a town near Nagar in the Khabur area.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPodany2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid_ez3ih5JgzUCpgPA57_57&#93;_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPodany2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid_ez3ih5JgzUCpgPA57_57]-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The campaign was headed by the Eblaite vizier <a href="/wiki/Ibbi-Sipish" title="Ibbi-Sipish">Ibbi-Sipish</a>, who led the combined armies to victory in a battle near <a href="/wiki/Terqa" title="Terqa">Terqa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELiverani2013&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0d1JAgAAQBAJpgPA123_123&#93;_51-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELiverani2013[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0d1JAgAAQBAJpgPA123_123]-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The alliance also attacked Armi and occupied it, leaving Ibbi-Sipish's son Enzi-Malik as governor.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOttoBiga2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA486_486&#93;_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOttoBiga2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA486_486]-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ebla suffered its first destruction a few years after the campaign,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBiga2014&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAcnmBQAAQBAJpgPA103_103&#93;_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBiga2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAcnmBQAAQBAJpgPA103_103]-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> probably following Isar-Damu's death.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStieglitz2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA219_219&#93;_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStieglitz2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA219_219]-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="First_destruction_of_Ebla">First destruction of Ebla</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ebla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: First destruction of Ebla"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The first destruction occurred <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2300</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>; palace "G" was burned, baking the clay tablets of the royal archives and preserving them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERistvet2014&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidVqERBgAAQBAJpgPA54_54&#93;_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERistvet2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidVqERBgAAQBAJpgPA54_54]-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many theories about the cause and the perpetrator have been posited:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBiga2014&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAcnmBQAAQBAJpgPA103_103&#93;_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBiga2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAcnmBQAAQBAJpgPA103_103]-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Akkadian_soldier_of_Naram-Sin.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Akkadian_soldier_of_Naram-Sin.jpg/220px-Akkadian_soldier_of_Naram-Sin.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="406" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Akkadian_soldier_of_Naram-Sin.jpg/330px-Akkadian_soldier_of_Naram-Sin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Akkadian_soldier_of_Naram-Sin.jpg/440px-Akkadian_soldier_of_Naram-Sin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1336" data-file-height="2464" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Akkadian_Empire" title="Akkadian Empire">Akkadian</a> soldier of <a href="/wiki/Naram-Sin_of_Akkad" title="Naram-Sin of Akkad">Naram-Sin</a>, with helmet and long sword, on the Nasiriyah stele. He carries a metal vessel of Anatolian type. From <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a>, Iraq, c. 2300 <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>. <a href="/wiki/Iraq_Museum" title="Iraq Museum">Iraq Museum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>
<ul><li><b>High (early) dating hypothesis</b>: <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Pettinato" title="Giovanni Pettinato">Giovanni Pettinato</a> supports an early dating for Ebla that would put the destruction at around 2500&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA61_61&#93;_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA61_61]-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Pettinato, while preferring the date of 2500&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>, later accepted the event could have happened in 2400&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA62_62&#93;_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA62_62]-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The scholar suggests the city was destroyed in 2400&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span> by a Mesopotamian such as <a href="/wiki/Eannatum" title="Eannatum">Eannatum</a> of Lagash – who boasted of taking tribute from Mari – or <a href="/wiki/Lugalzagesi" class="mw-redirect" title="Lugalzagesi">Lugalzagesi</a> of <a href="/wiki/Umma" title="Umma">Umma</a>, who claimed to have reached the Mediterranean.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA62_62&#93;_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA62_62]-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>Akkadian hypothesis</b>: Both kings <a href="/wiki/Sargon_of_Akkad" title="Sargon of Akkad">Sargon of Akkad</a> and his grandson <a href="/wiki/Naram-Sin_of_Akkad" title="Naram-Sin of Akkad">Naram-Sin</a> claimed to have destroyed a town called Ibla,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGurney2003&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidRtMSrGe8MY0CpgPA119_119&#93;_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGurney2003[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidRtMSrGe8MY0CpgPA119_119]-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The discoverer of Ebla, <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Matthiae" title="Paolo Matthiae">Paolo Matthiae</a>, considers Sargon a more likely culprit;<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA68_68&#93;_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA68_68]-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> his view is supported by <a href="/wiki/Trevor_R._Bryce" title="Trevor R. Bryce">Trevor Bryce</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBryce2014&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidq8Z7AgAAQBAJpgPA16_16&#93;_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBryce2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidq8Z7AgAAQBAJpgPA16_16]-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but rejected by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Astour" title="Michael Astour">Michael Astour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA70_70&#93;_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA70_70]-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The conquest of <a href="/wiki/Armanum" title="Armanum">Armanum</a> and Ebla on the Mediterranean coast by Naram-Sin is mentioned in several of his inscriptions:<sup id="cite_ref-DF132_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF132-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1244412712">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 32px}.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;margin-top:0}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{padding-left:1.6em}}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"Whereas, for all time since the creation of mankind, no king whosoever had destroyed Armanum and Ebla, the god Nergal, by means of (his) weapons opened the way for Naram-Sin, the mighty, and gave him Armanum and Ebla. Further, he gave to him the Amanus, the Cedar Mountain, and the Upper Sea. By means of the weapons of the god Dagan, who magnifies his kingship, Naram-Sin, the mighty, conquered Armanum and Ebla."</p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8202;<cite>Inscription of Naram-Sin. E&#160;2.1.4.26<sup id="cite_ref-DF132_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DF132-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>
<ul><li><b>Mari's revenge</b>: According to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alfonso_Archi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alfonso Archi (page does not exist)">Alfonso Archi</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Biga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Maria Biga (page does not exist)">Maria Biga</a>, the destruction happened approximately three or four years after the battle of Terqa.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBiga2014&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAcnmBQAAQBAJpgPA103_103&#93;_58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBiga2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAcnmBQAAQBAJpgPA103_103]-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Archi and Biga say the destruction was caused by Mari<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBiga2014&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAcnmBQAAQBAJpgPA103_103&#93;_58-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBiga2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAcnmBQAAQBAJpgPA103_103]-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> in retaliation for its humiliating defeat at Terqa.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPodany2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid_ez3ih5JgzUCpgPA59_59&#93;_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPodany2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid_ez3ih5JgzUCpgPA59_59]-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This view is supported by <a href="/wiki/Mario_Liverani" title="Mario Liverani">Mario Liverani</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELiverani2013&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0d1JAgAAQBAJpgPA123_123&#93;_51-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELiverani2013[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0d1JAgAAQBAJpgPA123_123]-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Archi says the Mariote king <a href="/wiki/Isqi-Mari" class="mw-redirect" title="Isqi-Mari">Isqi-Mari</a> destroyed Ebla before ascending the throne of his city.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBretschneiderVan_VyveLeuven2009&#91;httpswwwacademiaedu645365War_of_the_lords_The_battle_of_chronology_7&#93;_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBretschneiderVan_VyveLeuven2009[httpswwwacademiaedu645365War_of_the_lords_The_battle_of_chronology_7]-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>Natural catastrophe</b>: Astour says a natural catastrophe caused the blaze which ended the archive period.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA74_74&#93;_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA74_74]-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He says the destruction was limited to the area of the royal palace and there is no convincing evidence of looting.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA74_74&#93;_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA74_74]-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He dates the fire to <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2290</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Middle_Chronology" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle Chronology">Middle Chronology</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA75_75&#93;_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA75_75]-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Second_kingdom">Second kingdom</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ebla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Second kingdom"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1257001546"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1043282317"><table class="infobox ib-country vcard"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above adr"><div class="fn org country-name">Second Eblaite Kingdom</div><div class="ib-country-names">Ebla</div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-subheader"><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2300</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>–<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2000</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><span class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Frameless"><a href="/wiki/File:Second_Eblaite_Empire.png" class="mw-file-description" title="Approximate borders of the second kingdom"><img alt="Approximate borders of the second kingdom" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Second_Eblaite_Empire.png/250px-Second_Eblaite_Empire.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="137" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Second_Eblaite_Empire.png/375px-Second_Eblaite_Empire.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Second_Eblaite_Empire.png/500px-Second_Eblaite_Empire.png 2x" data-file-width="1028" data-file-height="564" /></a></span><div class="ib-country-map-caption">Approximate borders of the second kingdom</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Capital</th><td class="infobox-data">Ebla</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Common&#160;languages</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Eblaite_language" title="Eblaite language">Palaeo-Syrian</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Government</th><td class="infobox-data">Monarchy</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Historical era</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1257001546"></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;Established </div></th><td class="infobox-data"><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2300</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;Disestablished </div></th><td class="infobox-data"><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2000</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The second kingdom's period is designated "Mardikh IIB2", and spans the period between 2300 and 2000&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatthiae2013a&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA38_38&#93;_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatthiae2013a[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA38_38]-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The second kingdom lasted until Ebla's second destruction, which occurred anytime between 2050 and 1950&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>, with the 2000&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span> dating being a mere formal date.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA78_78&#93;_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA78_78]-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBryce2014&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidq8Z7AgAAQBAJpgPA324_324&#93;_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBryce2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidq8Z7AgAAQBAJpgPA324_324]-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Akkadian_Empire" title="Akkadian Empire">Akkadians</a> under <a href="/wiki/Sargon_of_Akkad" title="Sargon of Akkad">Sargon of Akkad</a> and his descendant <a href="/wiki/Naram-Sin_of_Akkad" title="Naram-Sin of Akkad">Naram-Sin</a> invaded the northern borders of Ebla aiming for the forests of the <a href="/wiki/Nur_Mountains" title="Nur Mountains">Amanus Mountain</a>; the intrusions were separated by roughly 90&#160;years and the areas attacked were not attached to Akkad.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA79_79&#93;_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA79_79]-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Archi accept that the Ibla mentioned in the annals of Sargon and Naram-Sin is the Syrian Ebla but do not consider them responsible for the destruction which ended the Archive period.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArchi2015&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidWHplCwAAQBAJpgPA26_26&#93;_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArchi2015[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidWHplCwAAQBAJpgPA26_26]-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By the time of Naram-Sin, Armi was the hegemonic city in northern Syria and was destroyed by the Akkadian king.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArchi2015&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidWHplCwAAQBAJpgPA471_471&#93;_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArchi2015[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidWHplCwAAQBAJpgPA471_471]-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ebla9.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Ebla9.JPG/220px-Ebla9.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Ebla9.JPG/330px-Ebla9.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Ebla9.JPG/440px-Ebla9.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption>Palace "P5"</figcaption></figure>
<p>A new local dynasty ruled the second kingdom of Ebla,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBryce2014&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidq8Z7AgAAQBAJpgPA16_16&#93;_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBryce2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidq8Z7AgAAQBAJpgPA16_16]-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but there was continuity with its first kingdom heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDolce2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA245_245&#93;_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDolce2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA245_245]-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ebla maintained its earliest features, including its architectural style and the sanctity of the first kingdom's religious sites.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDolce2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA252_252&#93;_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDolce2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA252_252]-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A new royal palace was built in the lower town,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA76_76&#93;_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA76_76]-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the transition from the archive period is marked only by the destruction of palace&#160;"G".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA74_74&#93;_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA74_74]-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Little is known about the second kingdom because no written material have been discovered aside from one inscription dating to the end of the period.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA76_76&#93;_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA76_76]-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The second kingdom was attested to in contemporaneous sources; in an inscription, <a href="/wiki/Gudea" title="Gudea">Gudea</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lagash" title="Lagash">Lagash</a> asked for cedars to be brought from <a href="/wiki/Urshu" title="Urshu">Urshu</a> in the mountains of Ebla, indicating Ebla's territory included Urshu north of <a href="/wiki/Carchemish" title="Carchemish">Carchemish</a> in modern-day Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA81_81&#93;_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA81_81]-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Texts that dates to the seventh year of <a href="/wiki/Amar-Sin" title="Amar-Sin">Amar-Sin</a> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2040</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> a ruler of the <a href="/wiki/Ur_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Ur III">Ur III</a> empire, mention a messenger of the <a href="/wiki/Ens%C3%AD" class="mw-redirect" title="Ensí">Ensí</a> ("Megum") of Ebla.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKlengel1992&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid5GptAAAAMAAJ_36&#93;_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKlengel1992[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid5GptAAAAMAAJ_36]-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The second kingdom was considered a vassal by the Ur III government,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA87_87&#93;_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA87_87]-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but the nature of the relation is unknown and it included the payment of tribute.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA132_132&#93;_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA132_132]-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A formal recognition of Ur's overlordship appears to be a condition for the right of trade with that empire.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA101_101&#93;_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA101_101]-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The second kingdom disintegrated toward the end of the <span class="nowrap">21st century <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>,</span><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA101_101&#93;_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA101_101]-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and ended with the destruction of the city by fire, although evidence for the event has only been found outside of the so-called "Temple of the Rock", and in the area around palace "E" on the acropolis.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDolce2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA252_252&#93;_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDolce2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA252_252]-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The reason for the destruction is not known;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDolce2010&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA252_252&#93;_88-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDolce2010[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid9bbgJzacoJYCpgPA252_252]-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> according to Astour, it could have been the result of a <a href="/wiki/Hurrian" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurrian">Hurrian</a> invasion <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2030</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamblin2006&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbiyDDd0uKGMCpgPT247_250&#93;_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamblin2006[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidbiyDDd0uKGMCpgPT247_250]-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> led by the former Eblaite vassal city of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ikinkalis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ikinkalis (page does not exist)">Ikinkalis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>note 12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA124_124&#93;_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA124_124]-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The destruction of Ebla is mentioned in the fragmentary Hurro-Hittite legendary epic "Song of Release" discovered in 1983,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBachvarova2009&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAnXbhhN_kpICpgPA66_66&#93;_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBachvarova2009[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAnXbhhN_kpICpgPA66_66]-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which Astour considers as describing the destruction of the second kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAstour2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA153_153&#93;_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAstour2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid0Rwals-oh6kCpgPA153_153]-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the epic, an Eblaite assembly led by a man called "Zazalla" prevents king <a href="/w/index.php?title=Meki_of_Ebla&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Meki of Ebla (page does not exist)">Meki</a> from showing mercy to prisoners from Ebla's former vassal Ikinkalis,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArchi2002&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksid5a8-NudlBx8CpgPA24_24&#93;_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArchi2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid5a8-NudlBx8CpgPA24_24]-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> provoking the wrath of the Hurrian storm god <a href="/wiki/Teshub" title="Teshub">Teshub</a> and causing him to destroy the city.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBachvarova2009&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAnXbhhN_kpICpgPA67_67&#93;_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBachvarova2009[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAnXbhhN_kpICpgPA67_67]-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Middle_Bronze">Middle Bronze</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ebla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Middle Bronze"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Third_kingdom">Third kingdom</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ebla&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Third kingdom"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1257001546"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1043282317"><table class="infobox ib-country vcard"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above adr"><div class="fn org country-name">Third Eblaite Kingdom</div><div class="ib-country-names">Ebla</div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-subheader"><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2000</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>–<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1600</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Capital</th><td class="infobox-data">Ebla</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Common&#160;languages</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Amorite_language" title="Amorite language">Amorite language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeiss1985&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidkMbpAAAAMAAJ_213&#93;_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeiss1985[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidkMbpAAAAMAAJ_213]-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Religion <div class="ib-country-religion"></div></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Canaanite_religion" title="Canaanite religion">Ancient Levantine religion</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Government</th><td class="infobox-data">Monarchy</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Historical era</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1257001546"></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;Established </div></th><td class="infobox-data"><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2000</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;Disestablished </div></th><td class="infobox-data"><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1600</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data">
<table style="width:95%; text-align:center; margin:0 auto; display:inline-table;">

<tbody><tr>
<td style="text-align:center; border:0; padding-bottom:0"><div id="before-after"></div></td>
<td style="text-align:center;border:0; padding-bottom:0;"><b>Succeeded by</b>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td style="vertical-align:top; text-align:center; border:0;">
</td>
<td style="vertical-align:top; text-align:center;border:0;">
<table style="width:92%; text-align:center; margin:0 auto; border:0;">

<tbody><tr>
<td style="border:0; padding:0; vertical-align:middle; text-align:right;"><a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites">Hittites</a>
</td>
<td style="border:0; padding:0; vertical-align:middle;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites"><img alt="AlterOrient2" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/AlterOrient2.png/50px-AlterOrient2.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="40" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/AlterOrient2.png/75px-AlterOrient2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/AlterOrient2.png/100px-AlterOrient2.png 2x" data-file-width="1394" data-file-height="1118" /></a></span>
</td></tr>









































</tbody></table>
</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ibbit-Lim.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Ibbit-Lim.png/220px-Ibbit-Lim.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="221" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Ibbit-Lim.png/330px-Ibbit-Lim.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a7/Ibbit-Lim.png 2x" data-file-width="343" data-file-height="345" /></a><figcaption>Statue fragment of <a href="/wiki/Ibbit-Lim" title="Ibbit-Lim">Ibbit-Lim</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The third kingdom is designated "Mardikh&#160;III"; it is divided into periods&#160;"A" (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;2000–1800</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>) and "B" (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1800–1600</span>&#160;<span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatthiae2013a&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA38_38&#93;_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatthiae2013a[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidAaZg0ypYrnQCpgPA38_38]-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In period&#160;"A", Ebla was quickly rebuilt as a planned city.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarmanşah2007&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidX2eomg9Y14ECpgPA75_75&#93;_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarmanşah2007[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidX2eomg9Y14ECpgPA75_75]-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The foundations covered the remains of Mardikh&#160;II; new palaces and temples were built, and new fortifications were built in two circles – one for the low city and one for the acropolis.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarmanşah2007&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidX2eomg9Y14ECpgPA75_75&#93;_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarmanşah2007[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidX2eomg9Y14ECpgPA75_75]-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The city was laid out on regular lines and large public buildings were built.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBryce2014&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidq8Z7AgAAQBAJpgPA25_25&#93;_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBryce2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidq8Z7AgAAQBAJpgPA25_25]-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHooks1990&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidgoq0VWw9rGICpgPA226_226&#93;_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHooks1990[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidgoq0VWw9rGICpgPA226_226]-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Further construction took place in period&#160;"B".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBryce2014&#91;httpsbooksgooglecombooksidq8Z7AgAAQBAJpgPA25_25&#93;_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBryce2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidq8Z7AgAAQBAJpgPA25_25]-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:HPIM3077.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/HPIM3077.JPG/220px-HPIM3077.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/HPIM3077.JPG/330px-HPIM3077.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/HPIM3077.JPG/440px-HPIM3077.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a><figcaption>The vizier palace</figcaption></figure>
